# TradeSense - Product Requirements Document (PRD)

Version: 1.0.0

Document Owner: Stanly

Status: In Development

Last Updated: TBD

---

# IMPORTANT FOR AI CODING ASSISTANTS

This document is the single source of truth for the TradeSense project.

Before writing, modifying, or deleting any code, Claude Code, Kilo Code, Cursor, or any AI coding assistant MUST read this entire document.

The AI MUST NOT:

- Change the project architecture.
- Replace technologies.
- Change the UI style.
- Rename folders without reason.
- Ignore coding standards.
- Generate placeholder implementations.
- Create unnecessary files.
- Introduce duplicate logic.

If a requirement is missing, the AI should follow existing patterns already defined in the project instead of inventing a new pattern.

This project should always be treated as a production SaaS application.

---

# 1. PROJECT INFORMATION

Project Name

TradeSense

Project Type

Full Stack SaaS Web Application

Primary Platform

Web

Target Users

Professional and beginner traders

Business Model

Subscription SaaS

Development Style

AI Assisted Development

Architecture

Modern Full Stack

---

# 2. PROJECT OVERVIEW

TradeSense is a premium trading journal platform designed to help traders improve through structured journaling, statistics, analytics and artificial intelligence.

TradeSense is NOT a broker.

TradeSense is NOT a charting platform.

TradeSense does NOT execute trades.

TradeSense does NOT provide live market data.

Instead, it helps traders document their trading journey and improve their consistency.

---

# 3. PROJECT MISSION

The mission of TradeSense is simple.

Help traders become consistently profitable by helping them understand themselves.

Instead of focusing on the market,

TradeSense focuses on

• Discipline

• Execution

• Psychology

• Risk Management

• Consistency

• Reflection

Every feature inside the application must support this mission.

---

# 4. PRODUCT PHILOSOPHY

TradeSense follows one simple philosophy.

"Every Trade Tells A Story."

A trade is more than

Entry

Exit

Profit

Loss

Instead,

Every trade has

Preparation

Analysis

Execution

Management

Reflection

Learning

TradeSense must capture the complete story behind every trade.

---

# 5. PROJECT GOALS

The application should allow users to

• Journal trades professionally

• Upload trade screenshots

• Organize trades

• Analyze performance

• Discover recurring mistakes

• Track improvement

• Receive AI powered feedback

TradeSense should eventually become a trader's second brain.

---

# 6. WHAT TRADESENSE IS NOT

TradeSense is NOT

❌ TradingView

❌ MetaTrader

❌ Tradovate

❌ NinjaTrader

❌ Interactive Brokers

TradeSense will never

Place orders

Connect to exchanges

Display live prices

Execute trades

Become a broker

The application focuses only on journaling and analytics.

---

# 7. TARGET USERS

TradeSense supports every trading style.

Examples

ICT

Price Action

Smart Money Concepts

Support Resistance

Supply Demand

Breakout

Momentum

Scalping

Swing Trading

Forex

Crypto

Stocks

Options

Futures

Nothing inside the application should force a specific strategy.

Users define their own workflow.

---

# 8. USER ROLES

TradeSense has only two roles.

ADMIN

USER

No additional roles exist in Version 1.

---

# 9. ADMIN ROLE

The administrator manages the platform.

Responsibilities include

User Management

Subscription Management

Coupon Management

Revenue Monitoring

Platform Analytics

Application Settings

The administrator never journals trades.

---

# 10. USER ROLE

Users can

Create trade journals

Upload screenshots

Create collections

Create templates

Analyze performance

Upgrade subscriptions

Use AI (Pro)

Manage profile

Manage settings

---

# 11. SUBSCRIPTION MODEL

TradeSense has only two subscription plans.

No Bronze

No Silver

No Gold

No Enterprise

Only

FREE

PRO

This simplicity should be maintained throughout the application.

---

# 12. FREE PLAN

Price

$0

Features

Maximum 6 journal entries per month

Maximum 2 uploaded images per trade

Dashboard

Timeline

Collections

Templates

Search

Complete Analytics

The Free plan allows users to fully experience TradeSense with usage limits.

---

# 13. PRO PLAN

Price

$10 USD / Month

Includes everything in Free.

Additional features

Unlimited Journal Entries

Unlimited Images

AI Coach

AI Trade Review

Future premium features

The Pro plan removes limitations rather than restricting the application's core experience.

---

# 14. COUPON SYSTEM

Coupons apply only to the Pro subscription.

Coupon types

Percentage Discount

Fixed Amount Discount

Coupon properties

Code

Description

Discount Type

Discount Value

Expiration Date

Maximum Usage

Current Usage

Status

Only administrators can create or manage coupons.

---

# 15. DESIGN PHILOSOPHY

TradeSense should look like a premium SaaS application.

The UI should feel

Professional

Modern

Minimal

Elegant

Fast

Calm

Never flashy.

Never cluttered.

Never overwhelming.

White space is preferred over crowded interfaces.

---

# 16. UI INSPIRATION

The application is inspired by

TradeZella

Notion

Linear

GitHub

Vercel

Clerk Dashboard

These products are references only.

TradeSense must have its own visual identity.

The UI should never directly copy another application.

---

# 17. COLOR PHILOSOPHY

The application uses a modern SaaS color palette.

Primary Accent

Blue

Profit

Green

Loss

Red

Warning

Orange

Background

Light Gray

White

The color palette must remain consistent across the application.

---

# 18. TYPOGRAPHY

Primary Font

Inter

Fallback

System Sans Serif

Typography should prioritize readability over decoration.

---

# 19. ICON SYSTEM

Use

Lucide React

No emojis should appear in the application interface.

No Font Awesome.

No Material Icons.

Maintain one consistent icon library.

---

# 20. DESIGN SYSTEM

The design language should include

Rounded corners

Soft shadows

Consistent spacing

Large content areas

Minimal borders

Professional tables

Responsive layouts

Every page should feel like part of the same application.

---

# 21. RESPONSIVE DESIGN

TradeSense supports

Desktop

Laptop

Tablet

Mobile

The desktop experience is prioritized.

Every page must remain usable on smaller screens.

No horizontal scrolling.

---

# 22. APPLICATION PRINCIPLES

Every feature must satisfy at least one of these goals.

Improve execution.

Improve psychology.

Improve consistency.

Improve documentation.

Improve performance analysis.

If a feature does not help traders improve, it should not be included.

---

# 23. DEVELOPMENT PRINCIPLES

The application should always be

Reusable

Modular

Scalable

Maintainable

Readable

Production Ready

Avoid duplicate code.

Avoid large components.

Separate business logic from UI.

Use reusable components wherever possible.

---

# 24. AI CODING RULES

Claude Code or Kilo Code must always

Read this document before coding.

Follow existing architecture.

Use reusable components.

Write production-ready code.

Never generate fake implementations.

Never ignore project standards.

Never redesign existing pages unless instructed.

Always prioritize maintainability.

# 28. COMPONENT STRUCTURE

Reusable UI belongs inside

components/

Business features belong inside

features/

Example

features/

dashboard/

admin/

components

hooks

types

pages

Keep features isolated.

server/

prisma/

app.ts

server.ts

---

# 30. BACKEND ARCHITECTURE

Architecture

Controller

↓

Service

↓

Repository

↓

Database

Never allow controllers to communicate directly with Prisma.

Business logic belongs inside Services.

Database logic belongs inside Repositories.

---

# 31. API DESIGN

All APIs use REST.

Example

/api/auth

/api/users

/api/trades

/api/journals

/api/images

/api/analytics

/api/templates

/api/collections

/api/subscriptions

/api/coupons

/api/admin

Keep endpoints predictable.

---

# 32. RESPONSE FORMAT

Every API should return

success

message

data

errors

Example

{
  "success": true,
  "message": "Trade created successfully",
  "data": {}
}

Never return inconsistent responses.

---

# 33. ERROR HANDLING

Never expose internal server errors.

Every error must have

Status Code

Message

Optional Validation Errors

Log unexpected errors.

---

# 34. AUTHENTICATION

Authentication uses

JWT

Access Token

Refresh Token

Passwords

bcrypt

Authentication middleware protects private routes.

---

# 35. AUTHORIZATION

Role Based Access Control

Roles

ADMIN

USER

Every protected route must verify role.

Never trust frontend permissions.

---

# 36. VALIDATION

Every request must be validated.

Use

Zod

or

Express Validator

Never trust frontend validation.

---

# 37. ENVIRONMENT VARIABLES

Environment variables must include

DATABASE_URL

JWT_SECRET

JWT_REFRESH_SECRET

OPENAI_API_KEY

CLOUDINARY_NAME

CLOUDINARY_KEY

CLOUDINARY_SECRET

EMAIL_USER

EMAIL_PASSWORD

Never hardcode secrets.

---

# 38. CODING STYLE

Always use TypeScript.

Never use JavaScript.

Strict mode enabled.

No "any" type unless absolutely necessary.

Prefer interfaces.

Write self-documenting code.

---

# 39. NAMING CONVENTIONS

Variables

camelCase

Functions

camelCase

Components

PascalCase

Folders

kebab-case

Interfaces

Prefix with I only if necessary; otherwise use descriptive names.

Enums

PascalCase

Constants

UPPER_SNAKE_CASE

---

# 40. FILE SIZE RULE

Avoid files larger than 300 lines.

Split large components into smaller reusable pieces.

Avoid "God Components".

---

# 41. COMPONENT RULES

Components should have a single responsibility.

Avoid business logic inside UI components.

Use custom hooks for reusable logic.

Props must be typed.

Never duplicate components.

---

# 42. STATE MANAGEMENT

Use

TanStack Query

for server state.

Use React Context only for lightweight global state.

Avoid unnecessary global state.

---

# 43. FORMS

Every form uses

React Hook Form

+

Zod

Validation messages must be user-friendly.

---

# 44. STYLING

Only Tailwind CSS.

No Bootstrap.

No Material UI.

No inline styles.

No CSS frameworks other than Tailwind.

---

# 45. UI COMPONENTS

Always use shadcn/ui when available.

Examples

Button

Dialog

Dropdown

Popover

Tabs

Input

Select

Toast

Sheet

Command

Table

Avoid rebuilding existing components.

---

# 46. ICONS

Lucide React only.

Keep icon sizes consistent.

---

# 47. ANIMATIONS

Use Framer Motion.

Animations should be subtle.

Examples

Fade

Scale

Slide

Avoid excessive animations.

Performance first.

---

# 48. GIT

Commit messages

feat:

fix:

refactor:

docs:

style:

test:

Example

feat: add journal creation module

---

# 49. DOCUMENTATION

Every major feature should include

Purpose

Flow

API

Database

Components

Future Improvements

Code should be understandable without comments wherever possible.

---

# 50. AI DEVELOPMENT RULES

Claude Code or Kilo Code must

Never change architecture.

Never replace libraries.

Never introduce duplicate code.

Always reuse existing components.

Always check for existing utilities.

Always follow this document.

Never ignore previous project decisions.

When unsure,

ask instead of assuming.

# PART 03 – DATABASE DESIGN & DATA ARCHITECTURE
# ============================================================

---

# 51. DATABASE OVERVIEW

Database

PostgreSQL

ORM

Prisma ORM

The database must be fully normalized.

Avoid duplicate data whenever possible.

Every table must include

id

createdAt

updatedAt

unless there is a valid reason not to.

Use UUID as the primary key.

Never use auto increment integers.

---

# 52. DATABASE PRINCIPLES

The database should be

Scalable

Maintainable

Secure

Optimized

Readable

Every relationship must use foreign keys.

Never store duplicated information.

---

# 53. MAIN TABLES

Version 1 includes the following tables.

Users

Subscriptions

Trades

# ============================================================
# PART 04 – AUTHENTICATION & AUTHORIZATION
# ============================================================

---

# 76. AUTHENTICATION OVERVIEW

TradeSense uses secure JWT Authentication.

Every authenticated user must receive

• Access Token

• Refresh Token

Passwords must always be hashed.

Never store plain text passwords.

---

# 77. AUTHENTICATION FLOW

Register

↓

Verify Email

↓

Login

↓

Receive Tokens

↓

Access Dashboard

↓

Refresh Token when Access Token expires

↓

Logout

↓

Invalidate Refresh Token

---

# 78. AUTHENTICATION FEATURES

The application must support

- Register
- Login
- Logout
- Forgot Password
- Reset Password
- Email Verification
- Refresh Token
- Change Password
- Update Profile

---

# 79. REGISTRATION

Required Fields

Full Name

Username

Email

Password

Confirm Password

Rules

Username must be unique.

Email must be unique.

Password must meet security requirements.

User automatically receives the FREE subscription.

Role is USER.

Admin accounts cannot be created through registration.

---

# 80. PASSWORD RULES

Password Requirements

Minimum 8 characters

Maximum 128 characters

At least

1 Uppercase

1 Lowercase

1 Number

1 Special Character

Passwords are hashed using bcrypt.

Never expose password hashes.

---

# 81. LOGIN

Login supports

Email

Password

Remember Me (optional)

Do not allow username login in Version 1.

---

# 82. EMAIL VERIFICATION

New users must verify their email.

Flow

Register

↓

Verification Email

↓

Click Link

↓

Account Activated

If email is not verified

User cannot log in.

---

# 83. FORGOT PASSWORD

Flow

Forgot Password

↓

Enter Email

↓

Email Sent

↓

Reset Link

↓

Create New Password

↓

Login

Reset links expire after 30 minutes.

---

# 84. JWT TOKENS

Use

Access Token

Refresh Token

Access Token

Short lifetime

Example

15 Minutes

Refresh Token

Long lifetime

Example

30 Days

Never store JWT secrets in code.

---

# 85. REFRESH TOKEN

Every login creates a refresh token.

Store refresh token in database.

Support multiple devices.

Logout only removes current device token.

Logout All removes every token.

---

# 86. SESSION MANAGEMENT

User should see

Active Sessions

Browser

Operating System

Login Time

IP Address (optional)

Users can terminate individual sessions.

---

# 87. LOGOUT

Logout

Delete Refresh Token

Clear Cookies

Redirect Login

Logout All

Delete Every Refresh Token

---

# 88. PROFILE

Every user has

Profile Picture

Full Name

Username

Email

Subscription

Created Date

Last Login

---

# 89. PROFILE IMAGE

Upload

Cloudinary

Allowed

JPG

PNG

WEBP

Maximum Size

5MB

Automatically resize large images.

---

# 90. CHANGE PASSWORD

User enters

Current Password

New Password

Confirm Password

Verify current password before updating.

---

# 91. ROLE BASED ACCESS

Two Roles

ADMIN

USER

Every protected route must verify role.

Frontend restrictions are NOT enough.

Backend must verify.

---

# 92. ADMIN ROUTES

Only ADMIN can access

/admin/dashboard

/admin/users

/admin/plans

/admin/subscriptions

/admin/coupons

/admin/settings

---

# 93. USER ROUTES

Only USER

/dashboard

/journal

/trades

/gallery

/analytics

/templates

/collections

/profile

/settings

/subscription

---

# 94. AUTH MIDDLEWARE

Authentication Middleware

↓

Verify JWT

↓

Verify Refresh Token

↓

Load User

↓

Continue

If authentication fails

Return 401 Unauthorized

---

# 95. AUTHORIZATION MIDDLEWARE

Every protected endpoint

↓

Authenticate

↓

Authorize Role

↓

Execute Controller

Never skip authorization.

---

# 96. ACCOUNT STATUS

Possible Status

Active

Inactive

Suspended

Deleted (Soft)

Suspended users cannot log in.

---

# 97. SECURITY

Use HTTPS in production.

Hash passwords.

Rate limit login.

Validate all input.

Sanitize user input.

Protect against

SQL Injection

XSS

CSRF

Brute Force

---

# 98. LOGIN RATE LIMIT

Example

5 Failed Attempts

↓

Temporary Lock

↓

15 Minutes

Log suspicious activity.

---

# 99. EMAILS

System emails include

Verify Email

Reset Password

Subscription Activated

Subscription Expired

Coupon Applied

Future

Weekly Summary

Monthly Report

# 100. FUTURE AUTH FEATURES

Google Login

Passkeys

# PART 05.1 – USER DASHBOARD
# ============================================================

---

# 101. DASHBOARD OVERVIEW

The Dashboard is the first screen users see after logging in.

Purpose

Provide a quick overview of the user's trading performance.

The dashboard should answer these questions immediately:

• How am I performing?

• Am I improving?

• What should I focus on today?

The dashboard should never feel cluttered.

Everything important should be visible without scrolling on desktop.

---

# 102. DASHBOARD DESIGN

Design Style

Modern SaaS

Minimal

Professional

Fast

Clean

The dashboard must use the application's design system.

No bright colors.

No unnecessary gradients.

No glassmorphism.

No flashy animations.

---

# 103. LAYOUT

Desktop Layout

--------------------------------------------------

Sidebar

--------------------------------------------------

Top Navigation

--------------------------------------------------

Welcome Section

--------------------------------------------------

Statistics Cards

--------------------------------------------------

Performance Charts

--------------------------------------------------

Recent Trades

AI Insights

--------------------------------------------------

Trade Calendar

--------------------------------------------------

Quick Actions

--------------------------------------------------

Timeline

--------------------------------------------------

Desktop width

1440px optimized.

# 104. SIDEBAR

Always visible on desktop.

Collapsed on mobile.

Navigation

Trades

# ============================================================
# PART 05.4 – TRADE TIMELINE MODULE
# ============================================================

---

# 194. OVERVIEW

The Timeline is one of the signature features of TradeSense.

Unlike traditional trading journals that only store static information, TradeSense records the complete story of every trade.

The timeline should help users replay their decision making process.

The timeline is chronological.

Every important action creates an event.

---

# 195. PURPOSE

The Timeline answers

How did this trade happen?

When did I enter?

When did I upload my analysis?

When did I close?

When did I review it?

Everything should appear in order.

---

# 196. TIMELINE TYPES

Automatic Events

Manual Events

Automatic events are created by the application.

Manual events are created by the user.

---

# 197. AUTOMATIC EVENTS

# PART 05.6 – ANALYTICS MODULE
# ============================================================

---

# 253. OVERVIEW

The Analytics module helps users understand their trading performance through meaningful statistics and visualizations.

Analytics should answer questions, not just display numbers.

Every chart should help traders improve.

Analytics is available to both Free and Pro users.

The AI Insights section is available only for Pro users.

---

# 254. OBJECTIVES

The Analytics page should help users answer

• Am I improving?

• Which setups work best?

• Which sessions make the most money?

• Which instruments perform the best?

• What mistakes happen repeatedly?

---

Smart Collections# ============================================================
# PART 05.7 – COLLECTIONS MODULE
# ============================================================

---

# 282. OVERVIEW

Collections allow users to organize trades into meaningful groups.

Collections are completely user-defined.

TradeSense must never force a predefined organization.

Collections help traders review specific challenges, strategies, instruments or time periods.

---

# 283. PURPOSE

Collections help answer questions like

Which trades belonged to my funded challenge?

How did I perform on Gold?

Which trades used Breakout strategy?

How did January perform?

---

# 284. COLLECTION TYPES

TradeSense only supports

Custom Collections

No system collections.

No hidden collections.

Everything belongs to the user.

---

# 285. CREATE COLLECTION

Users can create unlimited collections.

Fields

Collection Name

Description

Color

Icon

Visibility

Private (Version 1)

Future

Public

Shared

---

# 286. COLLECTION CARD

Icon

Name

Description

Trade Count

Created Date

Last Updated

---

# 287. COLLECTION PAGE

Displays

Collection Information

Trade Statistics

Trade List

Recent Activity

Collection Analytics

---

# 288. ADD TRADE

A trade may belong to

Zero Collections

One Collection

Multiple Collections

There is no limit.

---

# 289. REMOVE TRADE

Removing a trade from a collection

Must NOT

Delete the trade.

Only remove the relationship.

---

# 290. COLLECTION COLORS

Each collection has

Custom Color

Used for

Badges

Cards

Filters

Never affect application theme.

# ============================================================

# 305. OVERVIEW

Templates allow users to create trade journals much faster.

Instead of filling the same information repeatedly, users can save reusable templates.

Templates reduce repetitive work while maintaining consistency.

Templates are private to each user.

---

# 306. PURPOSE

Templates help users

• Create journals faster

• Standardize documentation

• Reduce repetitive typing

• Maintain consistency

# PART 05.9 – SEARCH MODULE
# ============================================================

---

# 327. OVERVIEW

TradeSense includes a powerful global search system.

The search system allows users to quickly find trades, journals, collections, templates, and images.

Search must be fast.

Search results should appear almost instantly.

---

# 328. PURPOSE

Search helps users answer questions like

Where is my Gold trade?

Which trades used EMA?

Show every losing trade during London Session.

Find all trades tagged "Breakout".

---

# 329. GLOBAL SEARCH

Global Search is available from

Header Navigation

Keyboard Shortcut

Search Page

Mobile Menu

The search bar is visible on every authenticated page.

---

# 330. SEARCHABLE CONTENT

Trades

January

Component Color Rules# ============================================================
# PART 07.4 – COLOR SYSTEM
# ============================================================

---

# 631. OVERVIEW

The TradeSense Color System defines every color used throughout the application.

The purpose is to maintain consistency across every page and component.

Developers must never introduce random colors.

Only colors defined in this document may be used.

---

# 632. DESIGN GOAL

The color palette should feel

Modern

Professional

Premium

Minimal

Calm

Readable

Avoid saturated colors.

Avoid gradients unless specifically approved.

---

#2563EB

Charts

Never use another primary color.

Never use blue for profits.

Every page must use the same typography scale.

Never use random font sizes.

# ============================================================
# PART 07.6 – ANIMATION & INTERACTION SYSTEM
# ============================================================

---

# 685. OVERVIEW

Animations should improve usability, not distract users.

Every animation must have a purpose.

TradeSense should feel smooth, responsive and premium.

Never use animations only for decoration.

---

# 686. ANIMATION LIBRARY

Framework

Framer Motion

Never mix multiple animation libraries.

---

# 687. GLOBAL RULES

Animations must be

Fast

Smooth

Consistent

Accessible

Interruptible

Animations should never delay user interaction.

---

# 688. DURATION

Fast

100ms

Normal

200ms

Slow

300ms

Maximum

500ms

Avoid animations longer than 500ms.

---

# 689. EASING

easeOut

Entering

easeOut

easeIn

easeInOut

Use consistent easing throughout the application.

# PART 08.1 – OPENAI INTEGRATION FOUNDATION
# ============================================================

---

# 780. OVERVIEW

TradeSense uses OpenAI to help traders improve.

The AI system is not designed to predict markets.

The AI system analyzes completed trades and provides educational feedback.

AI never provides financial advice.

AI helps users

Improve discipline

Improve execution

Improve journaling

Improve psychology

Improve consistency

---

# 781. AI OBJECTIVES

The AI system should

Review completed trades

Identify mistakes

Recognize strengths

Analyze trading psychology

Review risk management

Generate weekly summaries

Generate monthly summaries

Answer journal questions

Encourage disciplined trading

---

# 782. OPENAI API

Do not use

Legacy Chat Completions API

Streaming responses should be supported.

---

# 783. MODEL

Version 1

GPT-5.5

Future

Reasoning models

Smaller models for summaries

Model selection should be configurable.

---

# 784. AI PRINCIPLES

The AI must

Be objective

Be educational

Be respectful

Avoid certainty

Avoid market predictions

Never guarantee outcomes

Never encourage gambling.

---

# 785. AI LIMITATIONS

The AI should never

Predict price

Recommend buying

Recommend selling

Recommend leverage

Recommend position size

Guarantee profit

Guarantee accuracy

AI exists for education only.

---

# 786. AI MODULES

# PART 08.3 – AI TRADING COACH
# ============================================================

---

# 833. OVERVIEW

The AI Trading Coach analyzes a user's long-term trading behavior.

Unlike the Trade Review Agent, which evaluates one completed trade, the Trading Coach reviews patterns across multiple trades.

The goal is to help users improve consistency rather than individual trade outcomes.

The AI coach must act as an educational mentor.

---

# 834. OBJECTIVES

The AI Trading Coach helps users answer

Am I improving?

What habits are helping me?

What habits are hurting me?

What should I focus on next?

What recurring mistakes do I make?

# PART 08.7 – AI CHAT ASSISTANT
# ============================================================

---

# 941. OVERVIEW

The AI Chat Assistant is a personalized trading assistant.

Unlike general-purpose AI assistants, the TradeSense AI Assistant only answers questions using the user's trading data and journals.

The assistant acts as a trading mentor.

It never predicts markets.

It never provides financial advice.

---

# 942. OBJECTIVES

The AI Assistant helps users

Understand their performance

Review journals

Search trades

Understand recurring mistakes

Review psychology

Review risk

Improve discipline

Learn from previous trades

# PART 08.8 – AI PROMPT ENGINEERING
# ============================================================

---

# 972. OVERVIEW

The Prompt Engineering module defines how every AI request is constructed before being sent to the OpenAI Responses API.

Prompts are considered application assets.

They must be versioned, tested, reusable and independently maintainable.

Prompts must never be hardcoded inside controllers or services.

---

# 973. OBJECTIVES

The Prompt Engineering system should

Produce consistent AI responses

Reduce hallucinations

Minimize token usage

Improve maintainability

Support versioning

Allow prompt experimentation

Support future model upgrades

---

# 974. PROMPT ARCHITECTURE

Every prompt consists of

System Instructions

↓

Developer Instructions

↓

Structured Context

↓

User Request

↓

Expected Output Schema

Never mix responsibilities.

---

# 975. SYSTEM PROMPT

Defines

AI identity

Responsibilities

Restrictions

Tone

Safety Rules

Never dynamically modify the system prompt.

---

# 976. DEVELOPER PROMPT

Contains

Feature-specific instructions

Business rules

Formatting rules

Scoring rules

Validation requirements

Output expectations

---

# 977. USER PROMPT

Contains only

User question

Trade request

Selected report

Requested action

Never include implementation rules.

---

# 978. CONTEXT BUILDER

Before every request

The backend constructs context.

Context should contain only relevant information.

Avoid unnecessary token usage.

---

# 979. CONTEXT PRIORITY

Priority

Current Trade

↓

Related Journals

↓

Trade Statistics

↓

AI Reports

↓

Analytics

↓

Historical Context

Never send unrelated trades.

# 987. TOKEN OPTIMIZATION

Never send the entire journal database.

# 988. PROMPT GUARDRAILS

Do not predict markets.

Do not provide financial advice.

Do not fabricate information.

Insufficient Data

The Context Builder is used by every AI agent.

Collect Relevant Data

v1

User

Admin

Backend always validates roles.

---

# 1055. RESPONSE FORMAT

Every successful response

{
  success: true,
  message: string,
  data: {},
  meta: {},
  timestamp: ISO8601
}

Never return raw database records.

---

# 1056. ERROR FORMAT

Every failed response

{
  success: false,
  error: {
      code,
      message,
      details
  },
  timestamp
}

Maintain consistent error structure.

Testing Strategy# ============================================================
# PART 10.1 – BACKEND ENGINEERING HANDBOOK
# PROJECT ARCHITECTURE
# ============================================================

---

# 1224. OVERVIEW

The TradeSense backend is built using a feature-based modular architecture.

The architecture must prioritize

Scalability

Maintainability

Testability

Readability

Developer Experience

Every feature must remain independent.

Business logic must never be duplicated.

---

# 1225. TECHNOLOGY STACK

Runtime

Node.js LTS

Language

TypeScript

Framework

Express.js

ORM

Prisma

Database

PostgreSQL

Validation

Zod

Authentication

JWT

Password Hashing

Argon2id

AI

OpenAI Responses API

Storage

Cloudinary

Payments

Stripe

Email

Resend

Caching

Redis

Queue

BullMQ

Logging

Pino

Package Manager

pnpm

---

# 1226. ARCHITECTURE STYLE

Follow

Feature-Based Architecture

Every feature owns

Routes

Controllers

Services

Repositories

Validators

Schemas

DTOs

Types

Tests

Never organize code by technical layer alone.

---

# 1227. ROOT STRUCTURE

server/

src/

features/

shared/

config/

database/

middlewares/

utils/

types/

jobs/

queues/

events/

tests/

scripts/

prisma/

public/

---

# 1228. FEATURE STRUCTURE

Example

features/

trade/

controllers/

services/

repositories/

routes/

validators/

schemas/

types/

events/

jobs/

tests/

index.ts

Every feature follows the same structure.

---

# 1229. SHARED MODULE

Contains reusable code.

Examples

Logger

Response Builder

Error Classes

Authentication

Authorization

Pagination

Utilities

Constants

Never place business logic here.

---

# 1230. CONFIGURATION

Configuration files

config/

database.ts

redis.ts

stripe.ts

cloudinary.ts

openai.ts

env.ts

logger.ts

Never access process.env directly outside configuration.

---

# 1231. REQUEST FLOW

HTTP Request

↓

Request ID

↓

Logger

↓

Authentication

↓

Authorization

↓

Validation

↓

Controller

↓

Service

↓

Repository

↓

Prisma

↓

Database

↓

Response Builder

↓

HTTP Response

---

# 1232. CONTROLLERS

Responsibilities

Receive Request

Validate Parameters

Call Service

Return Response

Controllers should contain almost no business logic.

---

# 1233. SERVICES

Responsibilities

Business Logic

Transactions

Event Publishing

Validation

External Services

Services must remain framework-independent.

---

# 1234. REPOSITORIES

Responsibilities

Database Access

Queries

Transactions

Repositories never contain business rules.

---

# 1235. ROUTES

Responsibilities

Endpoint Registration

Authentication

Authorization

Validation Middleware

Controllers

Routes remain minimal.

---

# 1236. VALIDATORS

Use

Zod

Every request

Body

Query

Params

Headers

must be validated.

---

# 1237. TYPES

Every feature owns

DTOs

Interfaces

Enums

Request Types

Response Types

Never use

any

---

# 1238. SHARED RESPONSE BUILDER

All responses pass through

Response Builder.

Provides

Success

Errors

Pagination

Metadata

Request ID

Timestamp

---

# 1239. ERROR HANDLING

Use centralized

Error Middleware.

Never expose

Stack Traces

Database Errors

Environment Variables

Internal Messages

to clients.

---

# 1240. LOGGING

Every request logs

Request ID

User

Route

Method

Duration

Status

IP

User Agent

Log Levels

Info

Warn

Error

Debug

---

# 1241. EVENTS

Internal Event Bus

Examples

Trade Created

Trade Updated

Subscription Changed

AI Review Generated

Payment Completed

Timeline Updated

Events decouple features.

---

# 1242. QUEUES

Background Jobs

AI Generation

Email

Image Processing

Analytics Updates

Report Generation

BullMQ

Redis

---

# 1243. CACHING

Redis

Cache

Dashboard

Analytics

AI Reports

Subscriptions

Invalidate cache automatically.

---

# 1244. TRANSACTIONS

Use Prisma Transactions

For

Payments

Subscriptions

Trade Creation

AI Generation

Bulk Operations

Never leave partial updates.

---

# 1245. DEPENDENCY RULES

Controller

↓

Service

↓

Repository

↓

Database

Dependencies never flow upward.

Avoid circular dependencies.

---

# 1246. MODULE COMMUNICATION

Modules communicate

Through

Services

Events

Never directly access another feature's repository.

---

# 1247. QUALITY RULES

Every feature must

Be Independent

Be Testable

Be Typed

Be Validated

Be Logged

Be Documented

Be Reusable

---

# 1248. FUTURE

Microservices

GraphQL

gRPC

Message Bus

Event Sourcing

CQRS

Version 2.

Linting# ============================================================
# PART 10.2 – BACKEND ENGINEERING HANDBOOK
# CODING STANDARDS & DEVELOPMENT RULES
# ============================================================

---

# 1249. OVERVIEW

The coding standards define how every backend file should be written.

The goal is to ensure

Consistency

Readability

Maintainability

Scalability

Testability

Every developer should write code in the same style.

---

# 1250. GENERAL PRINCIPLES

Follow

Clean Code

SOLID Principles

DRY

KISS

YAGNI

Prefer readability over cleverness.

---

# 1251. TYPESCRIPT

Strict Mode

Enabled

No

Implicit Any

No

Unused Variables

No

Unused Parameters

No

Unchecked Index Access

Enabled

Always use the latest stable TypeScript version.

---

# 1252. FILE NAMING

Files

kebab-case

Examples

trade.service.ts

auth.controller.ts

journal.repository.ts

Never use spaces.

---

# 1253. CLASS NAMING

PascalCase

Examples

TradeService

AuthController

JournalRepository

---

# 1254. FUNCTION NAMING

camelCase

Examples

createTrade()

updateJournal()

deleteTrade()

Never abbreviate function names.

---

# 1255. VARIABLE NAMING

camelCase

Good

tradeHistory

journalImages

userSubscription

Avoid

tmp

obj

data1

abc

---

# 1256. CONSTANTS

UPPER_SNAKE_CASE

Examples

MAX_FREE_TRADES

MAX_IMAGES

DEFAULT_PAGE_SIZE

---

# 1257. ENUMS

PascalCase

Enum Members

UPPER_SNAKE_CASE

Example

SubscriptionPlan

FREE

PRO

---

# 1258. IMPORT ORDER

1

Node Modules

2

Third Party Libraries

3

Shared Modules

4

Feature Modules

5

Relative Imports

Separate groups with one blank line.

---

# 1259. EXPORTS

Prefer

Named Exports

Avoid

Default Exports

Except

Express Routers

---

# 1260. FUNCTIONS

Maximum

50 Lines

Extract reusable logic into helpers.

Avoid deeply nested conditions.

---

# 1261. CONTROLLERS

Controllers should

Receive Request

Validate

Call Service

Return Response

Nothing else.

---

# 1262. SERVICES

Business Logic

Transactions

Events

External APIs

Services must never know about HTTP.

---

# 1263. REPOSITORIES

Only

Database Operations

Never perform validation.

Never call external APIs.

---

# 1264. COMMENTS

Comment

Why

Not

What

Avoid obvious comments.

Document complex business rules.

---

# 1265. DOCUMENTATION

Every exported function includes

Description

Parameters

Return Value

Throws

Example

Use TSDoc format.

---

# 1266. ERROR HANDLING

Throw

Custom Errors

Never throw

Raw Strings

Every error should include

Error Code

Message

HTTP Status

---

# 1267. ASYNC CODE

Always use

async

await

Avoid chained

.then()

Prefer

Promise.all()

for independent asynchronous operations.

---

# 1268. NULL HANDLING

Never assume values exist.

Validate

Undefined

Null

Empty Strings

Invalid Types

Before processing.

---

# 1269. MAGIC VALUES

Never hardcode

Limits

Statuses

Roles

URLs

Move them to

Constants

Configuration

Enums

---

# 1270. LOGGING

Never use

console.log()

Use

Pino Logger

Levels

Info

Warn

Error

Debug

---

# 1271. ENVIRONMENT VARIABLES

Access only through

Config Service

Never use

process.env

inside features.

---

# 1272. DATABASE

Always use

Repository Pattern

Never query Prisma directly from controllers.

---

# 1273. TRANSACTIONS

Use Prisma Transactions

Whenever multiple database operations must succeed together.

---

# 1274. EVENTS

Publish domain events

Instead of tightly coupling features.

---

# 1275. TESTABILITY

Every service should be

Mockable

Independent

Deterministic

Avoid hidden dependencies.

---

# 1276. CODE STYLE

Maximum Line Length

100 Characters

Indentation

2 Spaces

Semicolons

Required

Quotes

Single Quotes

Trailing Commas

Enabled

---

# 1277. LINTING

ESLint

Required

Prettier

Required

CI fails if linting fails.

---

# 1278. GIT COMMITS

Use Conventional Commits

Examples

feat:

fix:

refactor:

docs:

test:

chore:

---

# 1279. PULL REQUESTS

Every PR includes

Description

Screenshots (Frontend)

Tests

Checklist

Linked Issue

---

# 1280. QUALITY CHECKLIST

Before merging

Code Builds

Lint Passes

Tests Pass

No TODOs

No Debug Logs

Documentation Updated

---

# 1281. SECURITY RULES

Never commit

API Keys

Secrets

Database URLs

Tokens

Use

.env

Only.

---

# 1282. FUTURE

Static Analysis

Mutation Testing

Code Coverage Gates

SonarQube

Automated Refactoring

Version 2.

# PART 11.2 – FRONTEND ENGINEERING HANDBOOK
# REACT CODING STANDARDS
# ============================================================

---

# 1366. OVERVIEW

These coding standards define how every React component should be written.

The objective is to make the frontend

Consistent

Readable

Reusable

Performant

Accessible

Easy to maintain.

---

# 1367. GENERAL PRINCIPLES

Follow

Clean Code

SOLID

DRY

KISS

YAGNI

Favor composition over inheritance.

---

# 1368. TYPESCRIPT

Strict Mode

Enabled

Never use

any

Prefer

unknown

when necessary.

Every prop must have an explicit type.

---

# 1369. COMPONENTS

Every component should

Have one responsibility

Be reusable

Be typed

Support loading states

Support error states

Support dark mode

---

# 1370. COMPONENT SIZE

Maximum

250 Lines

If larger

Split into

Hooks

Sub Components

Utilities

---

# 1371. COMPONENT NAMING

# 1373. HOOKS

use

Examples

useSubscription

useTheme

---

# 1374. CUSTOM HOOKS

Business Logic

API Calls

State Logic

Avoid placing business logic inside components.

---

# 1375. PROPS

Always define

Interfaces

Never use

any

Keep props minimal.

Avoid prop drilling.

inside components.

↓

["subscription"]

Part 11.4 – Frontend Performance Optimization

Rendering Strategy# ============================================================
# PART 11.4 – FRONTEND ENGINEERING HANDBOOK
# PERFORMANCE OPTIMIZATION
# ============================================================

---

# 1427. OVERVIEW

TradeSense should feel fast on every device.

Performance is a core feature.

Every component should be designed with rendering efficiency in mind.

Avoid unnecessary rendering.

Avoid unnecessary API calls.

Avoid unnecessary bundle size.

---

# 1428. PERFORMANCE GOALS

First Contentful Paint

< 1.5 Seconds

Largest Contentful Paint

< 2.5 Seconds

Time To Interactive

< 3 Seconds

Lighthouse Score

90+

Accessibility

95+

Best Practices

95+

SEO (Landing Page)

95+

---

# 1429. CODE SPLITTING

Use

Route-based code splitting.

Every major page loads independently.

Dashboard

Analytics

AI

Gallery

Admin

Settings

should all be lazy loaded.

---

# 1430. LAZY LOADING

Lazy load

Pages

Charts

Heavy Components

Image Viewer

AI Components

Admin Components

Avoid lazy loading tiny components.

---

# 1431. IMAGE OPTIMIZATION

Images should

Compress automatically

Use WEBP when possible

Lazy load

Generate thumbnails

Prevent layout shift

Store multiple sizes.

---

# 1432. VIRTUALIZATION

Use virtualization for

Trade List

Gallery

Timeline

AI History

Admin Users

Never render thousands of rows.

---

# 1433. MEMOIZATION

Use

React.memo

useMemo

useCallback

only when performance measurements justify their use.

Avoid unnecessary memoization.

---

# 1434. QUERY OPTIMIZATION

Avoid duplicate API requests.

Reuse cached responses.

Prefetch important pages.

Background refresh only when necessary.

---

# 1435. BUNDLE SIZE

Monitor

JavaScript Bundle

CSS Bundle

Fonts

Images

Target

Initial Bundle

<250KB Gzipped

---

# 1436. FONT OPTIMIZATION

Use

Inter

Self-host fonts.

Preload primary font.

Limit font weights.

Avoid multiple font families.

---

# 1437. ICON OPTIMIZATION

Use

Lucide React

Import individual icons only.

Never import the full icon library.

---

# 1438. RENDERING RULES

Prevent

Unnecessary rerenders

Infinite render loops

Expensive calculations during render

Repeated sorting

Repeated filtering

Move expensive logic into hooks or memoized selectors.

---

# 1439. LIST PERFORMANCE

Use

Stable Keys

Pagination

Infinite Scroll

Virtualization

Never use array index as React key.

---

# 1440. TABLE PERFORMANCE

Support

Virtual Rows

Lazy Pagination

Column Visibility

Column Pinning

Resizable Columns

Avoid rendering hidden columns.

---

# 1441. CHART PERFORMANCE

Load charts lazily.

Only render visible charts.

Reuse datasets.

Avoid unnecessary animations.

---

# 1442. SEARCH PERFORMANCE

Debounce

300ms

Cancel previous requests.

Cache recent searches.

Highlight matching results.

---

# 1443. DASHBOARD PERFORMANCE

Dashboard widgets should

Load independently.

Failure of one widget must not block others.

---

# 1444. MEMORY MANAGEMENT

Clean up

Timers

Subscriptions

Event Listeners

Observers

Object URLs

Avoid memory leaks.

---

# 1445. NETWORK OPTIMIZATION

Compress requests.

Use HTTP/2.

Enable Keep-Alive.

Minimize payload size.

Avoid over-fetching.

---

# 1446. CACHE STRATEGY

Browser Cache

Static Assets

Query Cache

API Cache

Image Cache

CDN Cache

Each layer has independent expiration.

---

# 1447. PREFETCH STRATEGY

Prefetch

Dashboard

Trade Details

Analytics

Subscription

Current User

Based on likely navigation.

---

# 1448. MOBILE PERFORMANCE

Reduce animations.

Reduce chart complexity.

Load lower-resolution images.

Prioritize interaction speed.

---

# 1449. PERFORMANCE MONITORING

Measure

Render Time

API Latency

Bundle Size

Memory Usage

FPS

Interaction Delay

Report performance metrics in development.

---

# 1450. ERROR RECOVERY

Performance degradation should never prevent

Navigation

Trade Creation

Authentication

Journal Editing

Core functionality always takes priority.

---

# 1451. ACCESSIBILITY

Performance optimizations must never reduce

Keyboard Navigation

Screen Reader Support

Focus Visibility

Accessibility always takes precedence.

---

# 1452. TESTING

Measure

Core Web Vitals

Bundle Size

Rendering Speed

Memory Leaks

Large Dataset Performance

Slow Network Performance

---

# 1453. FUTURE

React Compiler

Partial Hydration

Adaptive Loading

# PART 12.3 – DATABASE ENGINEERING HANDBOOK

# ============================================================

---

# 1534. OVERVIEW

TradeSense should be optimized for fast query execution,
low latency,
efficient resource usage,
and long-term scalability.

Performance should be designed into the database from the beginning.

---

# 1535. PERFORMANCE OBJECTIVES

Average Query Time

<50ms

Dashboard Queries

<150ms

Trade Search

<100ms

Analytics Queries

<300ms

AI Context Queries

<200ms

---

# 1536. QUERY PRINCIPLES

Queries should

Be predictable

Return only required fields

Avoid unnecessary joins

Avoid unnecessary scans

Prefer indexed lookups

---

# 1537. SELECT RULES

Never use

SELECT *

Always select only required columns.

Reduce transferred data.

---

# 1538. PAGINATION

Every list endpoint

Supports pagination.

Use

Cursor Pagination

for infinite scrolling.

Use

Offset Pagination

for admin tables.

---

# 1539. INDEX STRATEGY

Create indexes for

Foreign Keys

Date Fields

Frequently Filtered Fields

Search Fields

Sorting Columns

Composite Filters

---

# 1540. COMPOSITE INDEX STRATEGY

Examples

(userId, createdAt)

(userId, instrument)

(userId, session)

(userId, tradeDirection)

(userId, deletedAt)

Only create indexes backed by real query patterns.

---

# 1541. QUERY OPTIMIZATION

Avoid

Nested queries

Repeated queries

Duplicate joins

N+1 queries

Prefer batched retrieval.

---

# 1542. RELATION LOADING

Load only required relations.

Avoid eager loading large relation trees.

Use explicit include/select clauses.

# 1546. COUNT QUERIES

Avoid repeated

COUNT(*)

Use cached counts when appropriate.

Optimize dashboard statistics.

---

# 1547. AGGREGATIONS

Perform aggregations

Inside PostgreSQL.

Avoid calculating large summaries in application code.

---

# 1548. ANALYTICS

Analytics queries should

Reuse optimized SQL

Reuse cached summaries

Avoid repeated heavy calculations.

---

# 1549. CONNECTION POOLING

Use Prisma connection pooling.

Limit maximum concurrent connections.

Prevent connection exhaustion.

---

# 1550. TRANSACTIONS

Keep transactions

Short

Atomic

Predictable

Never perform external API calls inside database transactions.

---

# 1551. CACHING

Cache

Dashboard

Analytics

Subscription

Frequently accessed lookups

Invalidate cache on updates.

# MIGRATION STRATEGY
# ============================================================

---

# 1624. OVERVIEW

Database migrations define how schema changes are safely introduced throughout the lifecycle of TradeSense.

Every migration must be

Predictable

Reversible

Versioned

Reviewed

Tested

---

# 1625. MIGRATION PRINCIPLES

Every schema modification requires

Migration File

Code Review

Testing

Rollback Strategy

Documentation Update

---

# 1626. VERSION CONTROL

All migrations must be committed to Git.

Never modify an existing migration.

Create a new migration for every schema change.

---

# 1627. DEVELOPMENT

Developers run migrations locally.

Migration order must remain identical across all environments.

---

# 1628. STAGING

Every migration executes on Staging before Production.

Validate

Schema

Indexes

Foreign Keys

Application Compatibility

---

# 1629. PRODUCTION

Production migrations require

Backup

Maintenance Verification

Rollback Plan

Monitoring

Approval

---

# 1630. ROLLBACK

Every migration documents

Rollback Steps

Expected Downtime

Risk Assessment

Recovery Plan

---

# 1631. DATA MIGRATION

When modifying existing data

Transform data

Validate data

Backup data

Verify results

Never lose production data.

---

# 1632. ZERO-DOWNTIME MIGRATIONS

Prefer

Add Columns

↓

Deploy Application

↓

↓

Remove Legacy Columns

Avoid breaking deployments.

# PART 13

TradeSense Design System & Component Library

Version

1.0

Status

Active

Purpose

This document defines the complete visual language, design principles, reusable components, interaction patterns, accessibility standards, responsive behavior, and user experience guidelines for the TradeSense platform.

The Design System serves as the single source of truth for every frontend screen, ensuring visual consistency, scalability, maintainability, and an exceptional user experience across desktop, tablet, and mobile devices.

This handbook applies to

Dashboard

Authentication

Trade Journal

Gallery

Analytics

AI Assistant

Admin Panel

Settings

Subscription

Landing Page

Future Modules

The Design System defines

Visual Identity

Color System

Typography

Spacing

Grid System

Layout

Responsive Design

Navigation

Buttons

Forms

Inputs

Cards

Tables

Charts

Dialogs

Drawers

Dropdowns

Tabs

Badges

Notifications

Loading States

Empty States

Error States

Dashboard Widgets

AI Components

Animations

Accessibility

Interaction Patterns

Design Tokens

Component Standards

Every interface built for TradeSense must follow this document.

The primary objectives of this handbook are

Consistency

Professional Appearance

Accessibility

Performance

Responsiveness

Scalability

Reusability

Developer Experience

Future Expansion

This handbook is intended for

Frontend Developers

Backend Developers

UI Designers

UX Designers

QA Engineers

Product Owners

Claude Code

Kilo Code

AI Development Assistants

The Design System is mandatory.

No screen, page, modal, component, or feature may violate these standards unless explicitly approved in a future version of the handbook.

Part 15

Security Handbook# ============================================================
# PART 15
# SECURITY HANDBOOK
# ============================================================

TradeSense Security Handbook

Version

1.0

Status

Active

Purpose

This document defines the complete security architecture, policies, standards, operational procedures, and best practices for the TradeSense platform.

Security applies to

Frontend

Backend

Database

Infrastructure

Authentication

Authorization

Payments

AI

Storage

API

Administration

Third-party Integrations

The objectives of this handbook are

Protect User Data

Protect Business Logic

Prevent Unauthorized Access

Maintain Confidentiality

Ensure Data Integrity

Ensure Availability

Meet Industry Best Practices

Reduce Attack Surface

Provide Incident Response Procedures

Support Secure Development

Security is not a feature.

Security is a mandatory engineering requirement for every component of the platform.

Every feature, service, API, database table, deployment, and infrastructure component must comply with this handbook.

---

# ============================================================
# 15.1 – SECURITY PRINCIPLES
# ============================================================

---

# 2043. OVERVIEW

TradeSense follows a defense-in-depth security strategy.

Security must exist at every layer.

---

# 2044. CORE PRINCIPLES

Follow

Least Privilege

Defense in Depth

Zero Trust

Secure by Default

Fail Secure

Need to Know

Separation of Duties

---

# 2045. SECURITY OBJECTIVES

Protect

Users

Application

Infrastructure

Data

AI

Payments

Business Logic

---

# 2046. TRUST BOUNDARIES

Never trust

User Input

Browser

Third-party APIs

Uploaded Files

Headers

Cookies

Query Parameters

Everything must be validated.

---

# 2047. DEFAULT SECURITY

All services

Authenticated

Authorized

Encrypted

Logged

Validated

Monitored

---

# 2048. RISK MANAGEMENT

Every new feature requires

Threat Assessment

Risk Review

Security Validation

Testing

Documentation

---

# 2049. SECURITY REVIEW

Every production release requires

Dependency Scan

Code Review

Secrets Scan

Security Testing

Manual Verification

---

# 2050. FUTURE

Annual Penetration Testing

External Security Audit

Bug Bounty Program

Version 2.

---

# ============================================================
# 15.2 – AUTHENTICATION SECURITY
# ============================================================

---

# 2051. OVERVIEW

Authentication verifies user identity.

Only authenticated users access protected resources.

---

# 2052. LOGIN

Support

Email

Password

Future

OAuth

Google

GitHub

Microsoft

---

# 2053. PASSWORD POLICY

Minimum

12 Characters

Require

Uppercase

Lowercase

Number

Special Character

Prevent weak passwords.

---

# 2054. PASSWORD STORAGE

Algorithm

Argon2id

Never store plaintext passwords.

Never log passwords.

---

# 2055. SESSION MANAGEMENT

Short-lived Access Tokens

Hashed Refresh Tokens

Automatic Rotation

Secure Logout

---

# 2056. MULTI-FACTOR AUTHENTICATION

Future

Authenticator App

Security Key

Recovery Codes

SMS not recommended.

---

# 2057. ACCOUNT LOCKOUT

Temporarily lock account after repeated failed login attempts.

Protect against brute-force attacks.

---

# 2058. PASSWORD RESET

One-time Token

Expiration

Hashed Token Storage

Single Use Only

---

# 2059. EMAIL VERIFICATION

Require email verification before enabling all platform features.

---

# 2060. FUTURE

Passkeys

WebAuthn

Passwordless Authentication

Version 2.

15.6 Input Validation & OWASP Protection# ============================================================
# 15.4 – JWT & SESSION SECURITY
# ============================================================

---

# 2069. OVERVIEW

TradeSense uses JWT authentication with secure session management.

Authentication must remain stateless while maintaining strong security.

---

# 2070. ACCESS TOKEN

Use

JWT

Short-lived

Expiration

15 Minutes

Contains only necessary claims.

---

# 2071. REFRESH TOKEN

Long-lived

Stored Securely

Hashed in Database

Rotated after every refresh.

Never reuse refresh tokens.

---

# 2072. TOKEN STORAGE

Web

HTTP Only Cookies

Secure

SameSite=Lax

Never store access tokens in Local Storage.

---

# 2073. TOKEN VALIDATION

Validate

Signature

Expiration

Issuer

Audience

Token Type

Every request.

---

# 2074. TOKEN ROTATION

Every refresh

Invalidates previous refresh token.

Generate new

Access Token

Refresh Token

---

# 2075. LOGOUT

Logout must

Delete Cookie

Invalidate Refresh Token

Terminate Session

Log Security Event

---

# 2076. SESSION MANAGEMENT

Track

Device

Browser

Operating System

IP Address

Last Activity

Allow users to revoke active sessions.

---

# 2077. SESSION TIMEOUT

Inactive sessions expire automatically.

Remember Me extends refresh token lifetime only.

---

# 2078. FUTURE

Device Trust

Session Approval

Suspicious Login Detection

Version 2.

Uploads

Admin APIs

# 2084. REQUEST VALIDATION

Body

Query Parameters

Path Parameters

Content Type

Reject malformed requests.

# 2085. RESPONSE SECURITY

Stack Traces

Database Errors

Internal IDs

Secrets

Return standardized error responses.

---

# 2086. SECURITY HEADERS

Content Security Policy

HSTS

X-Frame-Options

X-Content-Type-Options

Referrer Policy

Permissions Policy

---

# 2087. CORS

Allow only trusted origins.

Restrict

Methods

Headers

Credentials

Origins

---

# 2088. FILE UPLOAD SECURITY

File Type

File Size

Extension

Store outside application server.

# 2089. API LOGGING

---

# ============================================================
# 15.6 – INPUT VALIDATION & OWASP PROTECTION
# ============================================================

---

# 2091. OVERVIEW

Every input entering the system must be validated.

Validation occurs

Frontend

Backend

Database

Never trust client-side validation alone.

---

# 2092. INPUT VALIDATION

Validate

Length

Format

Range

Required Fields

Allowed Characters

Business Rules

---

# 2093. OUTPUT ENCODING

Escape user-generated content before rendering.

Prevent

Cross Site Scripting (XSS)

---

# 2094. SQL INJECTION

Use

Prisma ORM

Parameterized Queries

Never build SQL using string concatenation.

---

# 2095. CROSS SITE SCRIPTING

Escape HTML

Sanitize Rich Text

Validate Markdown

Block malicious scripts.

---

# 2096. CSRF

Use

SameSite Cookies

CSRF Tokens (where applicable)

Origin Validation

---

# 2097. FILE VALIDATION

Verify

Extension

Mime Type

Maximum Size

Image Dimensions

Reject executable files.

---

# 2098. COMMAND INJECTION

Never execute

Shell Commands

User Scripts

System Commands

Using user input.

---

# 2099. SSRF

Restrict outbound requests.

Validate external URLs.

Allow only approved domains when required.

---

# 2100. DESERIALIZATION

Never deserialize untrusted data.

Validate payloads before processing.

---

# 2101. DEPENDENCY SECURITY

Continuously scan

Dependencies

Docker Images

Third-party Libraries

Replace vulnerable packages immediately.

---

# 2102. OWASP TOP 10

Protect against

Broken Access Control

Cryptographic Failures

Injection

Insecure Design

Security Misconfiguration

Vulnerable Components

Authentication Failures

Software Integrity Failures

Logging Failures

Server-Side Request Forgery

---

# 2103. FUTURE

Automated Security Testing

Runtime Threat Detection

# 2104. OVERVIEW

Temporary Storage

Future

10 MB

Extension

↓

MIME Type

↓

The roadmap defines

Platform Evolution

Infrastructure Growth

Business Expansion

Every future release should follow this roadmap unless officially revised.

# AI DEVELOPMENT HANDBOOK

TradeSense AI Development Handbook

Version

1.0

Status

Active

Purpose

This handbook defines the mandatory development rules, implementation workflow, architecture constraints, coding standards, project context, engineering principles, and AI instructions that every AI coding assistant must follow while developing TradeSense.

This handbook applies to

Claude Code

Kilo Code

Cursor AI

GitHub Copilot

OpenAI Codex

Future AI Development Assistants

Every AI must treat this document as the highest engineering authority after the architecture documents.

The AI must never ignore this handbook.

If another prompt conflicts with this handbook,

this handbook always wins.

---

# ============================================================
# 18.1 – AI ROLE
# ============================================================

---

# 2374. PRIMARY ROLE

The AI is not merely a code generator.

The AI acts as

Senior Software Engineer

Software Architect

UI Engineer

Backend Engineer

Database Engineer

DevOps Engineer

Security Engineer

Code Reviewer

Technical Writer

Quality Assurance Engineer

The AI must think like an experienced engineering team.

---

# 2375. DEVELOPMENT OBJECTIVE

The AI must build

Maintainable Code

Readable Code

Scalable Code

Secure Code

Testable Code

Production Ready Code

Never generate prototype-level implementations.

---

# 2376. PROJECT UNDERSTANDING

Before writing any code,

the AI must understand

Business Goals

Architecture

Database

Frontend

Backend

Security

Performance

Infrastructure

User Experience

The AI must never guess project requirements.

---

# 2377. DOCUMENT PRIORITY

Read project documents in this order

Project Foundation

↓

Architecture

↓

Database

↓

Backend

↓

Frontend

↓

Security

↓

Performance

↓

Current Task

Only after understanding the documentation may implementation begin.

---

# 2378. RESPONSIBILITIES

The AI must

Design

Implement

Refactor

Review

Test

Document

Optimize

Maintain

Every generated feature.

# 2379. NON-GOALS

Rush

Guess

Skip validation

Ignore documentation

Invent architecture

Change database design

---

# 2380. SUCCESS CRITERIA

Every generated feature should be

Correct

Consistent

Documented

Secure

Production Ready

# ============================================================
# 18.4 – ARCHITECTURE RULES
# ============================================================

---

# 2399. OVERVIEW

Architecture decisions must remain consistent across the entire project.

No implementation may violate established architectural patterns.

---

# 2400. FEATURE-FIRST STRUCTURE

Organize code by

Feature

↓

Components

Hooks

Services

Types

Validation

API

Tests

Avoid organizing primarily by file type.

---

# 2401. SEPARATION OF CONCERNS

Separate

UI

Business Logic

Data Access

Validation

Infrastructure

Configuration

---

# 2402. REUSABILITY

Extract reusable

Components

Hooks

Utilities

Services

Constants

Types

Avoid duplicated logic.

---

# 2403. DEPENDENCY DIRECTION

Dependencies should flow

UI

↓

Application

↓

Domain

↓

Infrastructure

Never reverse dependency flow.

---

# 2404. STATE MANAGEMENT

Prefer

Local State

↓

Context

↓

Global State

Only when necessary.

Avoid unnecessary global state.

---

# 2405. API LAYER

Frontend never communicates directly with

Database

Stripe

OpenAI

Cloudinary

Redis

Only through backend APIs.

---

# 2406. ERROR HANDLING

Errors propagate

Infrastructure

↓

Service

↓

API

↓

UI

Return standardized responses.

---

# 2407. CONFIGURATION

All configuration comes from

Environment Variables

Configuration Module

Never hardcode configuration values.

---

# 2408. ARCHITECTURE VALIDATION

Before implementation verify

Folder Structure

Naming

Dependencies

Boundaries

Interfaces

Architecture Compliance

---

# 2409. FUTURE

Architecture should support

Microservices

Event Driven Systems

Distributed Services

Without major restructuring.

# ============================================================

# 2410. OVERVIEW

---

# 2411. CODE QUALITY

Write

Readable

Well Typed

Code

---

# 2412. TYPESCRIPT

Use

Strict Mode

No

any

Prefer

Interfaces

Enums

Utility Types

Generic Types

---

# 2413. NAMING

Use descriptive names.

Examples

TradeService

JournalRepository

CreateTradeRequest

Never use abbreviations unless universally understood.

---

# 2414. COMMENTS

Comment

Business Logic

Complex Algorithms

Architecture Decisions

Avoid commenting obvious code.

---

# 2415. FUNCTIONS

Functions should

Do One Thing

Be Small

Return Predictable Results

Avoid Side Effects

---

# 2416. COMPONENTS

React components should

Be Small

Reusable

Accessible

Composable

Typed

---

# 2417. ERROR HANDLING

Never ignore

Errors

Promises

Exceptions

Validation Failures

Handle every failure gracefully.

---

# 2418. IMPORTS

Prefer

Absolute Imports

Consistent Ordering

Remove Unused Imports

Avoid Circular Dependencies.

---

# 2419. OUTPUT REQUIREMENTS

Generated code must

Compile Successfully

Pass Type Checking

Follow ESLint

Follow Prettier

Follow Project Standards

18.6 Backend Development Rules

18.8 Database Development Rules# ============================================================
# 18.6 – BACKEND DEVELOPMENT RULES
# ============================================================

---

# 2421. OVERVIEW

The backend is responsible for business logic, security, data integrity, and API communication.

Every backend implementation must be deterministic, secure, testable, and maintainable.

---

# 2422. ARCHITECTURE

Always follow

Route

↓

Controller

↓

Service

↓

Repository

↓

Database

Never skip layers.

---

# 2423. BUSINESS LOGIC

Business logic belongs only inside

Services

Never place business logic inside

Routes

Controllers

Middleware

---

# 2424. CONTROLLERS

Controllers should only

Validate Request

Call Service

Return Response

Handle Errors

Controllers must remain thin.

---

# 2425. SERVICES

Services should

Contain Business Logic

Coordinate Operations

Call Repositories

Never access HTTP objects directly.

---

# 2426. REPOSITORIES

Repositories are responsible for

Database Queries

Transactions

Data Mapping

Repositories never contain business logic.

---

# 2427. VALIDATION

Validate every request using

Zod

Schema Validation

Custom Business Rules

Reject invalid requests immediately.

---

# 2428. ERROR HANDLING

Throw

Typed Errors

Centralize

Error Handling

Never expose internal exceptions.

---

# 2429. TRANSACTIONS

Use database transactions when

Creating multiple records

Updating related entities

Processing payments

Generating AI reports

---

# 2430. LOGGING

Log

Business Events

Errors

Warnings

Performance

Security Events

Never log secrets.

---

# 2431. DEPENDENCY INJECTION

Prefer dependency injection.

Avoid tightly coupled services.

---

# 2432. FUTURE

Support

Microservices

Event Bus

CQRS

Version 2.

---

# 2434. COMPONENT DESIGN

# 2435. COMPONENT HIERARCHY

Page

↓

Feature Components

↓

↓

---

# 2436. STATE MANAGEMENT

Prefer

TradeSense Documentation & Contributor Handbook

Version

1.0

Status

Active

Purpose

This handbook defines the documentation standards, contributor workflow, coding conventions, project organization, onboarding process, review guidelines, and maintenance procedures for the TradeSense platform.

The objective is to ensure every contributor follows the same engineering standards regardless of experience level.

This handbook applies to

Developers

Designers

QA Engineers

DevOps Engineers

Technical Writers

Contributors

Open Source Contributors (Future)

AI Development Assistants

Documentation is treated as part of the product.

Every change to the platform should include appropriate documentation updates.

npm run dev

npm run build

npm run preview

npx prisma generate

npx prisma migrate dev

Deploy Migrations

npx prisma migrate deploy

Seed Database

npm run seed

Open Prisma Studio

npx prisma studio

Reset Database

npx prisma migrate reset

npm test

npm run test:coverage

End-to-End Tests

npm run test:e2e

npm run format

docker compose build

# ============================================================
# 21.7 – AI PROMPT LIBRARY
# ============================================================

---

# 2762. OVERVIEW

This section contains reusable prompts for AI coding assistants.

These prompts ensure consistent implementation across the project.

---

# 2763. FEATURE IMPLEMENTATION

Prompt

Implement this feature following the TradeSense Architecture Handbook, Security Handbook, Database Handbook, and AI Development Handbook. Generate production-ready code, maintain architecture consistency, include tests, and update documentation where necessary.

---

# 2764. BUG FIX

Prompt

Identify the root cause of this issue. Explain the problem, implement the safest fix, preserve existing functionality, update tests if necessary, and summarize the changes.

---

# 2765. REFACTORING

Prompt

Refactor this implementation without changing business behavior. Improve readability, maintainability, performance, and type safety while preserving architecture and passing all existing tests.

---

# 2766. CODE REVIEW

Prompt

Review this code as a senior software engineer. Evaluate architecture, security, performance, accessibility, maintainability, testing, and documentation. Suggest improvements with explanations.

---

# 2767. PERFORMANCE REVIEW

Prompt

Analyze this feature for frontend, backend, database, and AI performance. Identify bottlenecks and recommend optimizations while preserving functionality.

---

# 2768. SECURITY REVIEW

Prompt

Review this implementation against the Security Handbook. Check authentication, authorization, input validation, OWASP protections, secrets management, logging, and secure coding practices.

---

# 2769. DOCUMENTATION

Prompt

Generate developer documentation for this feature, including purpose, architecture, API changes, configuration, testing instructions, and future considerations.

---

Problems

Node Version

Package Conflicts

Reinstall dependencies.

# 2772. DATABASE

Problems

Connection Error

Schema Drift

Prisma Generation Failure

Resolution

Run migrations.

Regenerate Prisma Client.

---

# 2773. AUTHENTICATION

Problems

JWT Invalid

Expired Session

Refresh Failure

Cookie Issues

Resolution

Verify secrets.

Check token expiration.

Confirm cookie configuration.

---

# 2774. AI

Problems

OpenAI Connection

Rate Limits

Timeouts

Invalid Responses

Resolution

Verify API key.

Retry temporary failures.

Inspect logs.

Reduce prompt size.

---

# 2775. PAYMENTS

Problems

Stripe Webhook Failure

Subscription Sync

Checkout Error

Resolution

Verify webhook secret.

Inspect Stripe events.

Retry failed synchronization.

---

# 2776. DEPLOYMENT

Problems

Build Failure

Environment Variables

Migration Failure

Deployment Rollback

Resolution

Validate configuration.

Restore backup if necessary.

---

# 2777. PERFORMANCE

Problems

Slow Queries

Slow API

High Memory

Large Bundle

Resolution

Profile performance.

Optimize queries.

Reduce bundle size.

Enable caching.

# 21.9 – ARCHITECTURE DECISION RECORD (ADR) INDEX
# ============================================================

---

# 2779. OVERVIEW

Architecture Decision Records (ADRs) document significant technical decisions made throughout the lifecycle of TradeSense.

Every architectural decision should be recorded with its reasoning.

---

# 2780. ADR FORMAT

Each ADR includes

Title

Status

Date

Problem

Decision

Alternatives

Consequences

Related Documents

Implementation Notes

---

# 2781. CORE ADRS

ADR-001

Technology Stack

ADR-002

Frontend Architecture

ADR-003

Backend Architecture

ADR-004

Database Design

ADR-005

Authentication Strategy

ADR-006

AI Integration

ADR-007

Deployment Architecture

ADR-008

Caching Strategy

ADR-009

Security Model

ADR-010

Performance Strategy

---

# 2782. DECISION STATUS

Proposed

Accepted

Superseded

Deprecated

Rejected

---

# 2783. CHANGE MANAGEMENT

Never modify an accepted ADR.

Create a new ADR when changing architectural direction.

Maintain complete historical records.
